● Now I have a clear picture of both projects. Here's my analysis and merge strategy:                                                                         u                                                                                                                                                       
  ---                                                                                                                                                        Merge Strategy: OSLRS Design System → VLPRS                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           What VLPRS Already Has (Good Foundation)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              - All 20 routes and page content in src/content/*.ts (CMS-ready)                                                                                           - Working shadcn/ui component library                                                                                                                      - Responsive nav with dropdown + mobile sheet                                                                                                              - Proper content structure (hero, sections, cards, accordion)                                                                                              - Tailwind CSS v4 with @theme tokens in globals.css                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 
  What the OSLRS Design Brings (The "Premium Feel")

  The visual upgrade comes from 5 specific things:

  1. Poppins + Inter dual-font system — Self-hosted, preloaded. Currently VLPRS uses Inter for everything. Adding Poppins for headings creates that        
  "designed" feel.
  2. Hero gradient blobs — Two blurred, semi-transparent circles behind the hero. Simple CSS, huge visual impact. Currently the hero is a flat
  bg-gradient-to-b from-slate-50.
  3. SectionWrapper pattern — Consistent py-16 lg:py-24 with alternating backgrounds (white/neutral-50). VLPRS already does this inline but it's
  inconsistent.
  4. FeatureCard with hover states — Icon badge in colored background + border-shifts-to-primary on hover + shadow deepens. Currently VLPRS cards are      
  static (no hover interaction).
  5. LCP-optimized hero shell — Pre-rendered HTML in index.html before React hydrates. Makes the page feel instant.

  What I Recommend (Practical Plan)

  Phase 1 — Design Tokens + Fonts (globals.css + index.html)
  - Copy OSLRS font files (Poppins woff2 + fonts.css) to public/fonts/
  - Add --font-brand: Poppins to globals.css
  - Add font preload to index.html
  - Add hero shell CSS for instant paint
  - Keep existing crimson palette (both are Oyo State — same maroon works)

  Phase 2 — Reusable Layout Components (3 new components)
  - Create SectionWrapper.tsx (replaces inline section padding everywhere)
  - Create SectionHeading.tsx (consistent Poppins H2 headings)
  - Create FeatureCard.tsx (icon + title + desc + CTA with hover effects)

  Phase 3 — Homepage Upgrade (biggest visual impact)
  - Add gradient blobs to hero section
  - Swap inline sections to use SectionWrapper/SectionHeading
  - Add FeatureCard hover states to capabilities/trust/who-serves cards
  - Add StepIndicator pattern to "How It Works"
  - Lazy-load below-fold sections

  Phase 4 — Header/Footer Polish
  - Add backdrop-blur frosted glass header (already partially there)
  - Upgrade footer to OSLRS-style with brand row
  - Add SkipLink for accessibility

  Phase 5 — Content Pages
  - Wrap all content pages in consistent SectionWrapper pattern
  - Apply Poppins to all page headings
  - Add card hover states everywhere

  What NOT to Copy

  - OSLRS navigation structure (VLPRS already has its own correct nav per FR77)
  - OSLRS page content (already have VLPRS-specific content)
  - OSLRS dark mode (not in VLPRS scope)
  - OSLRS API/auth boilerplate (VLPRS already has its own server)
  - shadcn/ui base components (already have them, just style tokens change)

  My Recommendation

  Start with Phase 1 + 2 + 3 as a single sprint. The fonts + hero blobs + SectionWrapper pattern will transform the look instantly. Phases 4-5 are polish.

● Good. Now I have the full picture. Here's the recap:

  ---
  Seed Script — What Was Said in the Code Review

  The code review flagged this as LOW #3:

  [AI-Review][LOW] Seed script log omits "38 loan records" per AC7 — loans skipped for Epic 2 [seed-demo.ts:139]

  Accepted deviation: dynamic counts are better than hardcoded; loan seed deferred to Epic 2.

  Why it was accepted

  AC7 in the story says:

  "And mock loan records (10-15 per seeded MDA) with realistic Naira amounts..."
  "And the seed script logs: 'Seeded 5 users, 63 MDAs, 38 loan records'"

  But the story's own guardrail (line 546) explicitly says:

  "DO NOT create a full loans table in the database — That's Epic 2. If needed for seed, create minimal schema or add a TODO."

  Since the loans table doesn't exist in schema.ts yet (only mdas, users, refreshTokens, auditLog), the seed script correctly skips loan seeding and leaves
   a TODO comment at line 135-136:

  // 4. Mock loan records — skipped (loans table not yet created, Epic 2 scope)
  // TODO: Seed mock loan records when loans table is created in Epic 2

  What the two seed scripts do

  1. seed-demo.ts (pnpm seed:demo) — Development/demo environments:
  - Reads DEMO_SEED_PASSWORD from env (fallback: DemoPass1)
  - Seeds 63 MDAs in a single transaction:
    - 3 "full" MDAs: Ministry of Health (HLT), Ministry of Education (EDU), Ministry of Works and Transport (WKT)
    - 60 "name-only" MDAs: real Oyo State MDA names (Finance, Agriculture, Justice, etc.)
    - Idempotent via onConflictDoNothing({ target: mdas.code })
  - Seeds 5 demo user accounts:
    - ag@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng — Accountant General (super_admin)
    - deputy.ag@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng — Deputy AG (super_admin)
    - admin@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng — Department Admin (dept_admin)
    - health.officer@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng — Health Officer (mda_officer, linked to HLT)
    - education.officer@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng — Education Officer (mda_officer, linked to EDU)
    - Idempotent via onConflictDoNothing({ target: users.email })
  - Logs dynamic counts: Seeded X users, Y MDAs
  - Whole operation wrapped in db.transaction()

  2. seed-production.ts (pnpm seed:prod) — Production environments:
  - Requires SUPER_ADMIN_EMAIL and SUPER_ADMIN_PASSWORD env vars (exits with error if missing)
  - Creates a single super_admin account
  - Idempotent: checks if email already exists before inserting
  - No MDAs seeded (those come from admin workflows in production)

  ---
  Thoughts — Making It Better

  Here's what I'd suggest improving when Epic 2 lands and the loans table exists:

  1. Loan seeding — When the loans table is created in Epic 2, the TODO at line 135 should be replaced with actual seed data: ~10-15 loans per full MDA    
  (HLT, EDU, WKT) = ~38 loan records with realistic Naira amounts, staff IDs, statuses (active, completed, defaulting), and proper date ranges.
  2. The MDA count is correct at 63 — 3 full + 60 name-only = 63 total, which matches the AC.
  3. The current seed script is solid — it uses transactions, idempotent upserts, dynamic counting, proper password hashing. No changes needed right now;  
  the loan gap is a deliberate deferral, not a bug.

  Want me to do anything else with the seed scripts, or shall we move on to the next story?

  SUPER_ADMIN_PASSWORD=<whatever you set>
  SUPER_ADMIN_FIRST_NAME=<whatever you set>
  SUPER_ADMIN_LAST_NAME=<whatever you set>

  Can you change it? — The current script only creates; it doesn't update. If you want to change the email or password on production, you have two options:

  - Option A: Update the .env on the Droplet with the new credentials, then run a SQL command to update the existing record directly
  - Option B: I add an --update mode to the production seed script so it can update the existing super admin's email/password when re-run

  I'd recommend Option B — it's safer and repeatable.

● Found it. The button's default variant uses bg-primary text-primary-foreground:

  default: "bg-primary text-primary-foreground hover:bg-primary/90",

  But in globals.css, there's no --color-primary or --color-primary-foreground defined. Tailwind v4 maps bg-primary to --color-primary — since it doesn't  
  exist, the buttons render with no background.

● All clean. Here's what was wrong and what was fixed:

  Root cause: globals.css defined brand colors (--color-crimson, --color-teal, etc.) but was missing the shadcn semantic tokens that the Button component  
  actually uses. In Tailwind v4, bg-primary resolves to --color-primary — which didn't exist, so buttons rendered with no background color.

  Added these missing tokens:

  ┌────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┐
  │             Token              │       Value       │            Used by            │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-primary                │ #9C1E23 (crimson) │ Default button background     │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-primary-foreground     │ #FFFFFF           │ Default button text           │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-secondary              │ #F1F5F9           │ Secondary button background   │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-secondary-foreground   │ #1E293B           │ Secondary button text         │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-destructive            │ #DC2626           │ Destructive button background │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-destructive-foreground │ #FFFFFF           │ Destructive button text       │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-input                  │ #E2E8F0           │ Outline button border         │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ --color-ring                   │ #9C1E23           │ General ring color            │
  └────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────┴───────────────────────────────┘

  Also fixed the button's focus ring from ring-ring (crimson) to ring-focus-ring (teal) for consistent accessibility focus indicators.

  Want me to commit and push this fix?

● I think I found the issue. Let me check the CORS and Vite proxy configuration.

● Found it. Two problems:

  1. CORS: The server uses cors() with no options (defaults to Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *), but the frontend fetch uses credentials: 'include'.        
  Browsers reject this combination — when credentials are included, the origin must be explicit, not *.
  2. No Vite proxy: The client hits http://localhost:3001/api directly (cross-origin from http://localhost:5173), so CORS applies.

  The fix is to configure CORS on the server to allow the Vite dev origin with credentials:

● That was the bug. The browser was silently blocking every login response because of a CORS misconfiguration.

  What was wrong: The server used cors() with no options, which sets Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *. But the frontend fetch uses credentials: 'include'    
  (needed for cookies/CSRF). Browsers enforce a strict rule: when credentials are included, the * wildcard is not allowed — the origin must be explicit. So
   every POST to /auth/login was succeeding on the server but the browser threw away the response.

  What I fixed: Configured CORS with:
  - Dev: allows http://localhost:5173 and http://127.0.0.1:5173
  - Production: uses CLIENT_ORIGIN env var (fallback: https://vlprs.oyo.gov.ng)
  - credentials: true — tells the browser it's safe to include cookies

  To test it now:
  1. Restart the server (pnpm --filter server dev or however you start it)
  2. Go to http://localhost:5173/login
  3. Login with ag@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng / DemoPass1

❯ Quick one sometimes when I click a button or link on the page, the page renders just fine but I am shown the footer of the page not the start of the     
   page. Why?                                                                                                                                              
  ⎿  ⧉ Selected 1 lines from docs\so_far.txt in Visual Studio Code

● That's a classic SPA (Single Page Application) issue. When you navigate between routes, React Router swaps the content but the browser keeps the scroll  
  position from the previous page. So if you were scrolled down on page A and click a link to page B, you land at the same scroll offset — often showing   
  the footer.

  The fix is a ScrollRestoration component that scrolls to top on route changes.

● Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Neither layout has scroll restoration. The fix is simple — add a ScrollToTop component that both layouts use:

       6   const { pathname } = useLocation();
       7
       8   useEffect(() => {
       9     window.scrollTo(0, 0);
      10   }, [pathname]);

  ⎿  Done (32 tool uses · 37.9k tokens · 58s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

● Here's the fastest way to get logged in. You have 3 options, ordered by speed:

  ---
  Option 1: Create Admin CLI (Fastest — 30 seconds)

  SSH into your droplet and run:

  ssh deploy@<DROPLET_IP>
  cd /opt/vlprs
  docker exec vlprs-server-1 pnpm user:create-admin --email awwallawl@gmail.com --name "Awwal Lawal"

  This will:
  - Check if the email already exists → if it does, it'll fail with a duplicate error
  - If it succeeds, it prints a temporary password in the terminal
  - You login with that password → it forces you to change it on first login

  If it says duplicate email exists, use Option 2 instead.

  ---
  Option 2: Direct SQL Password Reset (If account exists but password broken)

  ssh deploy@<DROPLET_IP>
  cd /opt/vlprs

  # First check if the account exists and its state:
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c "SELECT email, is_active, failed_login_attempts, locked_until FROM users WHERE LOWER(email) = 
  'awwallawl@gmail.com';"

  If it shows the account is locked (failed_login_attempts >= 5), just clear the lockout:

  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c "UPDATE users SET failed_login_attempts = 0, locked_until = NULL WHERE LOWER(email) =
  'awwallawl@gmail.com';"

  Then try logging in again with your original password.

  If you need a new password entirely, generate a bcrypt hash and update it:

  # Generate hash inside the server container (has bcrypt available)
  docker exec vlprs-server-1 node -e "
  const bcrypt = require('bcrypt');
  bcrypt.hash('YourNewPassword123!', 12).then(h => console.log(h));
  "

  # Then update (replace HASH_OUTPUT with the hash from above)
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c "UPDATE users SET hashed_password = 'HASH_OUTPUT', failed_login_attempts = 0, locked_until =  
  NULL, must_change_password = false WHERE LOWER(email) = 'awwallawl@gmail.com';"

  ---
  Option 3: Update .env and Re-seed (Clean approach going forward)

  Edit /opt/vlprs/.env on the droplet:

  SUPER_ADMIN_EMAIL=awwallawl@gmail.com
  SUPER_ADMIN_PASSWORD=YourChosenPassword123!
  SUPER_ADMIN_FIRST_NAME=Awwal
  SUPER_ADMIN_LAST_NAME=Lawal

  Then run:

  docker exec vlprs-server-1 pnpm seed:prod

  Note: The seed is idempotent — if the email already exists, it skips (doesn't update the password). So this only works if the account doesn't exist 
  yet, or you delete it first.

  ---
  My Recommendation

  Start with Option 2 — run the diagnostic query first to see if the account exists and whether it's locked out. Most likely your account got locked  
  after multiple failed login attempts (5 attempts = 15 min lockout). Clearing the lockout might be all you need.

  If the account is gone entirely, use Option 1 (pnpm user:create-admin) — it's the cleanest and gives you a fresh temporary password in seconds.     

  Going forward, for a proper admin email: update the .env on the droplet with the correct SUPER_ADMIN_EMAIL and SUPER_ADMIN_PASSWORD so it survives  
  any future database resets.

● Found it. Here's the root cause:

  The demo seed (seed-demo.ts) is NEVER run automatically. When pnpm dev starts, it only starts the database container and the server — but no seed   
  data is loaded. So every time the Docker volume gets wiped (via docker compose down -v, Docker Desktop restart, WSL reset, etc.), your users table  
  is empty and login returns 401 because the user literally doesn't exist.

  The 401 isn't "wrong password" — it's "user not found in database."

  Let me fix this permanently by auto-seeding in development mode when the database is empty.

● Now I see the full root cause. Here's what's happening:

  pnpm dev → starts DB container + server, but NEVER seeds the database.

  When the Docker volume gets wiped (by docker compose down -v, Docker Desktop restart, WSL reset, docker system prune), the tables exist but are     
  completely empty. Login returns 401 because the user record literally doesn't exist — not wrong password, the user row is gone.

  Every time I "fixed" it, I was giving you credentials or re-running the seed manually. Then the volume gets wiped again, and you're back to square  
  one.

  The fix: Auto-seed on dev server startup when the users table is empty.

● Here's the full summary:
                                                                                                                                                      
  ---                                                                                                                                                   Root Cause                                                                                                                                          
                                                                                                                                                        The demo seed (pnpm seed:demo) was never called automatically. Your pnpm dev command only starts the DB container + server — it never seeds the       database. So whenever the Docker volume gets wiped (via docker compose down -v, Docker Desktop restart, WSL reset, docker system prune, etc.), the    users table ends up completely empty. The 401 wasn't "wrong password" — the user record literally didn't exist.                                     

  I confirmed this just now: SELECT count(*) FROM users; returned 0.

  What I Fixed

  1. Auto-seed on dev server startup (devAutoSeed.ts)

  When the server starts in NODE_ENV=development, it now:
  - Checks if the users table has any rows
  - If empty, automatically runs the demo seed (63 MDAs + 5 users)
  - If the tables don't exist at all (fresh volume), runs drizzle-kit push first
  - Logs the demo credentials in the terminal so you always know them

  2. Extracted reusable seed function (seed-demo.ts)

  Refactored the seed script so the core logic (runDemoSeed()) is an exported function that can be called both from the CLI (pnpm seed:demo) and from 
  the auto-seed module.

  3. Wired into server startup (index.ts)

  Added the auto-seed call after the server starts, gated behind NODE_ENV === 'development'. Production is unaffected.

  What This Means

  You will never hit this issue again locally. Every time you run pnpm dev, if the database is empty, it auto-seeds. You'll see this in the server    
  logs:

  devAutoSeed: users table is empty — seeding demo data...
  devAutoSeed: seeded 5 users, 63 MDAs
  devAutoSeed: demo credentials — email: ag@vlprs.oyo.gov.ng, password: DemoPass1

  For the Live Website

  The production server does NOT auto-seed (intentionally — production should never have demo data). For the live site, you need to SSH in and use the
   commands I outlined earlier (Option 1/2/3 from my previous message). The createAdmin CLI is the cleanest approach for production.

❯ What do you advice in order to have an admin account on the live website  

● Based on your infrastructure, here's what I recommend:

  Best Approach: createAdmin CLI (one command, secure)

  SSH into your droplet and run:

  ssh deploy@<DROPLET_IP>
  cd /opt/vlprs
  docker exec vlprs-server-1 pnpm user:create-admin --email awwallawl@gmail.com --name "Awwal Lawal"

  This will:
  1. Create a super_admin account with your email
  2. Generate a temporary password and print it in the terminal
  3. Set mustChangePassword = true — you'll be forced to set a proper password on first login
  4. Log the action in the audit trail

  Copy the temporary password from the terminal output and login immediately.

  Why This Is Better Than What You Did Before

  ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │            Before (one-off script)            │               Now (CLI tool)                │
  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Hardcoded hashed password in a committed file │ Password generated at runtime, never in git │
  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ No audit trail                                │ Logged as USER_CREATE_SUPER_ADMIN           │
  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ No forced password change                     │ Forces password change on first login       │
  ├───────────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Breaks if DB is recreated                     │ Can re-run anytime                          │
  └───────────────────────────────────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  If the Account Already Exists

  If awwallawl@gmail.com is already in the production DB (from the old script), the CLI will tell you "duplicate email." In that case, reset the      
  password instead:

  # Check if the account exists and its state
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c \
    "SELECT email, is_active, failed_login_attempts, locked_until FROM users WHERE LOWER(email) = 'awwallawl@gmail.com';"

  Then either:
  - If locked (failed_login_attempts >= 5): clear the lockout
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c \
    "UPDATE users SET failed_login_attempts = 0, locked_until = NULL WHERE LOWER(email) = 'awwallawl@gmail.com';"
  - If password is wrong/forgotten: reset it via the server container
  docker exec vlprs-server-1 node -e "
    import('bcrypt').then(b => b.hash('YourNewPassword123!', 12).then(h => console.log(h)))
  "
  # Copy the hash, then:
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c \
    "UPDATE users SET hashed_password = '<PASTE_HASH>', failed_login_attempts = 0, locked_until = NULL WHERE LOWER(email) = 'awwallawl@gmail.com';"   

  Going Forward

  Also update your /opt/vlprs/.env with:
  SUPER_ADMIN_EMAIL=awwallawl@gmail.com
  SUPER_ADMIN_PASSWORD=<a-strong-password>
  SUPER_ADMIN_FIRST_NAME=Awwal
  SUPER_ADMIN_LAST_NAME=Lawal

  This way, if the production DB is ever recreated, running docker exec vlprs-server-1 pnpm seed:prod will restore your admin account from the env    
  vars.

● Found the issue. The production Docker image is a slim node:22-alpine build — it only has the compiled dist/index.js and production node_modules. No
   pnpm, no tsx, no TypeScript source files.

  Quick fix right now — use direct SQL via the database container:

  # 1. Generate a bcrypt hash inside the server container (node IS available)
  docker exec vlprs-server-1 node -e "
  const bcrypt = require('bcrypt');
  bcrypt.hash('YOUR_PASSWORD_FROM_ENV', 12).then(h => console.log(h));
  "

  Replace YOUR_PASSWORD_FROM_ENV with the actual password from your .env file. Copy the hash output, then:

  # 2. Insert the admin account (replace PASTE_HASH with the hash from step 1)
  docker exec vlprs-db-1 psql -U vlprs -d vlprs_prod -c "
  INSERT INTO users (id, email, hashed_password, first_name, last_name, role, is_active, must_change_password, failed_login_attempts, created_at,     
  updated_at)
  VALUES (gen_random_uuid(), 'awwallawl@gmail.com', 'PASTE_HASH', 'Awwal', 'Lawal', 'super_admin', true, false, 0, NOW(), NOW())
  ON CONFLICT (email) DO UPDATE SET hashed_password = EXCLUDED.hashed_password, failed_login_attempts = 0, locked_until = NULL, is_active = true;     
  "

  The ON CONFLICT clause means: if the email already exists, it resets the password, clears any lockout, and ensures the account is active.

● This is a CI test failure. The authRoutes.test.ts cleanup fails because audit_log rows still reference users when the test tries to delete users.   
  The TRUNCATE audit_log is likely being blocked by the immutability trigger. Let me fix this.

● Searched for 2 patterns, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Found the issue. The trigger is a row-level BEFORE UPDATE OR DELETE trigger, so TRUNCATE bypasses it fine. But there's a race condition: the auth   
  service uses fire-and-forget audit logging (void logAuthEvent(...)), so async audit writes from a previous test can land after TRUNCATE audit_log   
  but before delete(users), causing the FK violation.

  The fix: use a single atomic TRUNCATE ... CASCADE for all tables. Let me check all test files with this pattern.

● Searched for 2 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

● 6 files with this pattern. Let me fix all of them by replacing the multi-step cleanup with a single atomic TRUNCATE CASCADE.

● Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

● I'll fix all 6 files by replacing the multi-step cleanup with a single atomic TRUNCATE ... CASCADE. This eliminates the race condition with
  fire-and-forget audit logging.

● Here's the answer:

  996 beneficiaries have null outstanding balance — their files don't include a balance column. The HTML stat cards were only counting the 3,758 with known  
  balances (3,193 Active + 565 Liquidated), silently dropping 996 people.

  The top offenders for missing balance data:
  - HIGH COURT: 292 — the "sec car loan" file format has no balance column
  - BIR: 232 — some BIR files lack balance
  - ACCOUNTANT GENERAL: 112
  - CSC: 74
  - EDUCATION: 65

  These 996 are all classified as Active (because the code sets status to "Liquidated" only when balance ≤ ₦100 — null balance defaults to Active).

  This is a data quality issue in those MDA file formats, not a pipeline bug. But the stat cards should show the full picture. Let me fix the HTML to show   
  all 4,754 with a separate "Balance Unknown" count:

● Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Now I see the full picture. Here's the gap you're hitting:

  The format mismatch is the real blocker

  Your legacy CD files are Excel files with 12-18 columns in varying formats across 4 eras. The submission pipeline accepts 8-column CSV only (Staff ID,     
  Month, Amount Deducted, Payroll Batch Reference, MDA Code, Event Flag, Event Date, Cessation Reason).

  These are two completely different formats. You can't upload 2019 CDU OYSG MDAs CAR LOAN DEDUCTION TEMPLATE.xlsx through the submission interface — it     
  would be rejected immediately.

  You actually have TWO pipelines built for different purposes

  ┌──────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┐    
  │     Pipeline     │           Built For           │                        Accepts                        │                 Creates                  │    
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤    
  │ Epic 3 Migration │ One-time legacy ingestion     │ Excel files, varying formats, intelligent column      │ Loan records + ledger baselines          │    
  │                  │                               │ mapping                                               │                                          │    
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤    
  │ Epic 5           │ Monthly operational           │ 8-column CSV only                                     │ Submission records, compared against     │    
  │ Submission       │ deductions                    │                                                       │ loans                                    │    
  └──────────────────┴───────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┘    

  The legacy CD files are deduction records — what was actually collected each month. Epic 3's migration pipeline was built to ingest exactly these files and
   create the loan baseline from them.

  What's remaining for your end-to-end test

  Step 1 — Run Epic 3 migration on a handful of legacy files (already built):
  - Log in as DEPT_ADMIN → navigate to migration interface
  - Upload a few CDU Excel files (e.g., Health, Agriculture, Secretariat)
  - Pipeline runs: column mapping → validation → person matching → baseline creation
  - Result: Loan records + ledger entries now exist in the DB for real staff IDs

  Step 2 — Create test submission CSVs (manual or scripted):
  - Take a few staff IDs from the migrated data
  - Create 8-column CSVs representing "this month's deductions"
  - This is what MDA officers would actually submit going forward

  Step 3 — Upload via submission interface (needs Story 11.0 period bypass):
  - Log in as MDA Officer or DEPT_ADMIN
  - Upload the test CSV
  - Comparison engine runs against the loan records from Step 1
  - See confirmation → comparison summary → history across all roles

  What Story 11.0 needs to add for this to work:
  - Task 3 (period bypass) — already scoped
  - New Task 5: A conversion utility that takes SQ-1's catalog.json output and generates 8-column submission CSVs from the legacy deduction records — so you 
  don't have to manually create test files

  Alternatively, we skip the conversion utility and you just create 2-3 small test CSVs by hand using staff IDs from the migrated data. That's 10 minutes of 
  work vs building a tool.

  The question for you: Have you already run the Epic 3 migration pipeline on any of these files? If not, that's actually Step 0 — and it's already built,   
  you just need to use it. If the migration interface has issues, we surface that in the combined retrospective.

  granularity becomes important later when you're tracking completeness across 63 MDAs × multiple years.

   to start verifying.

❯ is there anything still missing on this quest to get an immediate functionality?

● Let me think through the full end-to-end flow with what's scoped:

  After 11.1 + 11.0a + 11.0b, your workflow is:

  1. DEPT_ADMIN → Migration Dashboard → "Upload Legacy Data" → upload CDU Excel files → loan records + baselines created → 11.0a fixes this navigation       
  2. Coverage Tracker shows which MDAs × months have data, gaps as CSV/PDF → 11.0b adds this
  3. DEPT_ADMIN → creates a few 8-column test CSVs → uploads via submission pipeline (historical periods accepted) → 11.0a enables this
  4. Comparison engine compares submissions against migrated loan records → already built
  5. AG Dashboard → real metrics from migrated data, drill-downs filtered by metric, fund total configurable → 11.0a fixes all three
  6. All roles see appropriate data (MDA Officer scoped, DEPT_ADMIN all, AG read-only) → already built + C2 fix

  I don't see a gap. The pieces connect:

  Legacy Excel → Migration Pipeline → Loan Records in DB
                                            ↓
  Test CSV → Submission Pipeline → Comparison Engine → Results
                                            ↓
  AG Dashboard ← real metrics ← loans + ledger + submissions
  Coverage Tracker ← migration records ← per MDA × per month

  The one operational step that's manual (not system): you'd create a few 8-column test CSVs using staff IDs from the migrated data to test the submission   
  flow. That's 10 minutes of work, not a feature gap.

  The only risk is untested edge cases when the migration pipeline hits specific legacy file formats — but that's exactly what your UAT will surface. The    
  pipeline was built from SQ-1's column mapping logic and tested against 7 representative fixtures. Real files might have surprises. That's expected and     
  healthy.

  You're good to go with the current scope. Continue with 11.1, then 11.0a and 11.0b will unlock your full testing capability.

❯ Maybe I missed it earlier, what happens to the seeded data?

● The seeded data stays — it doesn't get removed or overwritten.

  What changes:
  - Story 11.0a Task 4 adds a scheme_fund_total config entry to the seed (so the AG dashboard shows "Fund Available" instead of "Awaiting Configuration") and
   ensures enough seed loans/ledger entries exist for meaningful drill-down results
  - When you run migration on real legacy files, the real data adds alongside the seed data — same tables, new rows

  The practical consideration:
  Once you start uploading real CDU data, the seed's 7 demo loans (fake staff IDs across Health/Education/Finance) will be mixed in with real records. The   
  dashboard metrics, drill-downs, and comparison engine will include both.

  For a clean UAT, you have two options:

  1. Leave seed data in — accept that the demo loans exist alongside real data. The numbers will be slightly inflated (7 extra loans, ~₦3M extra exposure).  
  Quick, no risk.
  2. Reset and re-seed with only real data — drop the demo loans after migration so the system contains only verified CDU records. Cleaner for showing to the
   AG, but means re-running seed for the MDA registry and user accounts (those need to stay).

  I'd recommend option 1 for now — leave it. Seven demo loans in a system with hundreds of real records is noise. You can clean them out later before        
  go-live. Keeps things simple while you're testing.

  Want me to note this decision in Story 11.0a?

❯ real CDU data- what does it mean. How do I clean the seeded data out as I dont want to forget this because the seeded data are real data and if I reupload 
 them again, it become an inflation and the is a Gov/Fin Tech App where figures integrity is highly important. Thoughts (make it better)                     

● You're absolutely right — and this is a critical point for a GovTech financial application. Let me be precise.

  "Real CDU data" = the files in docs/legacy_cd/

  The 125+ Excel files from the Car Loan Department archive — actual historical deduction records from real MDAs, real staff, real amounts. When you upload  
  these via migration, they become loan records and ledger entries in the database.

  The seed data problem

  The seed data includes 7 fabricated loans with fake staff IDs and fake amounts across Health, Education, and Finance MDAs. If these stay in the system:    

  - Dashboard shows ₦3M+ in fake exposure mixed with real figures
  - Fake staff IDs appear in the Master Beneficiary Ledger alongside real people
  - If a fake staff ID accidentally matches a real one, the comparison engine produces corrupt results
  - The AG sees numbers that don't reconcile with reality

  For a system where every Naira must be accountable, this is unacceptable.

  What should happen

  The seed contains two types of data:

  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┐
  │                    Keep                     │            Remove             │
  ├─────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ 63 MDA registry entries (real MDAs)         │ 7 demo loans (fake)           │
  ├─────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Admin user accounts (Awwal, AG, DEPT_ADMIN) │ Demo ledger entries (fake)    │
  ├─────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Scheme config entries                       │ Demo MDA officer users (fake) │
  ├─────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Role definitions                            │ Any demo submission records   │
  └─────────────────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────┘

  The right approach: Add a purge-demo-data script to Story 11.0a that cleanly removes all fabricated financial records while preserving the MDA registry and
   admin accounts. Run it once before uploading any real data. It should log exactly what was removed for the audit trail.

  Let me add this to Story 11.0a Task 4 now.

  What the live database needs on day one:

  1. You (DEPT_ADMIN) log in → upload legacy files via migration → real loan records created
  2. AG sets the scheme fund total
  3. MDA Officers are invited via user admin (Story 1.9a — already built)

  5. Dashboard reflects only real, verified data from day one

❯ On the live website all metrics are 0 so we have no seeded data on the live website. So I beleive we make the changes locally and it would be reflected on 
 the live website or what is your thought on this. Thoughts (make it better)                                                                                 

● That's actually good news — your live DB is already clean. No purge needed there.

  But there's an important distinction:

  Code vs Data — they travel differently

  ┌────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │              What              │              How it reaches live              │                            Example                            │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Code changes (features, fixes) │ Push to git → CI/CD deploys automatically     │ Story 11.0a drill-down fix, scheme fund dialog, period bypass │
  ├────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Data (uploads, configuration)  │ Done manually on each environment, separately │ Legacy file uploads, scheme fund amount, user accounts        │
  └────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Code changes you make locally WILL reach the live website — once pushed and deployed, the new features (upload button, drill-down filtering, period bypass,
   coverage tracker) are available on both local and live.

  Data you upload locally will NOT appear on live. Your local DB and the production DB are separate. Legacy files uploaded locally stay local. You'd upload  
  them again on the live site.

  The practical workflow

  Phase 1 — Local testing:
  1. Finish 11.1 → build 11.0a + 11.0b
  2. Test locally: purge seed data → upload a few legacy files → verify everything works
  3. Fix any issues found

  Phase 2 — Go live:
  1. Push code → CI/CD deploys to live
  2. Log in to live as DEPT_ADMIN
  3. Upload legacy files via Migration Dashboard (live DB is already clean — zero data, no purge needed)
  4. AG logs in → sets scheme fund total
  5. Invite MDA Officers → they verify their data
  6. System is live with real data only

  The purge script from Task 4 is a local dev tool only — production never had seed data, so it doesn't need purging. I'll note that distinction in the      
  story. Want me to update it?
